VoxQube is a new IT service for content localization based on the symbiosis of artificial and natural intellect. Machines answer for accuracy and speed when transcribing, translating and providing voice-over, while a person ensures that all authentic, real-life intonations are preserved during the recording and editing process.
How to Teach a Robot to Speak with Human Intonations
Speech recognition technology transcribes the sound from the original recording or video and transforms it into text; the neuro-networks then translate the recording into any required language; speech synthesis programs re-voice the content â€” now using a selected voice and in a new language. This process is monitored by a synthesis designer â€” a specialist who is well-versed in both localization and sound editing. They check translation accuracy, apply any necessary corrections before beginning to implement the new voice, and then edit the resulting audio track to make it sound like a real-life voice: this is done by raising and lowering voice tone, introducing pauses, and adding intonations where appropriate.
The VoxQube neuro-networks possess in their arsenal many languages of the world: amongst them there is Polish, Portuguese, Brazilian, German and Arabic. Content can be voiced with different options â€” male and female, as well and childrenâ€™s and teenagers voices. The project library totals more than 200 different voices, each of which will produce a sound that is as natural as possible.
